<t7691>HISTORICAL NOTES</t7691>
<t7692>HISTORICAL NOTES ABOUT THE STORY</t7692>
<t7693>OF THE MAID</t7693>
<t7694>Partial transcription of the minutes of the Twelfth Symposium on Gileadean Studies, held as part of the International Historical Association Congress that took place at the University of Denay, Nunavit, on June 25, 2191.</t7694>
<t7695>President: Professor Maryann Crescent Moon (Maryann Luna Creciente) from the Department of Caucasian Anthropology at the University of Denay, Nunav it.</t7695>
<t7696>Inaugural Speaker: Professor James Darcy Pieixoto, Director of the Twentieth and Twenty-First Century Archives, University of Cambridge, England.</t7696>
<t7697>CRESCENT MOON:</t7697>
<t7698>I am delighted to welcome you all, and pleased to see that many of you are attending the undoubtedly fascinating and beneficial lecture by Professor Pieixoto.</t7698> <t7699>The members of the Gileadean Research Association believe that this period deserves more thorough study, as it was responsible for altering the world map, especially in this hemisphere.</t7699>
<t7700>But before moving on to that, I would like to make some announcements.</t7700> <t7701>The fishing expedition will depart tomorrow, as scheduled, and for those who have not brought adequate rain gear and insect repellent, I inform you that you can obtain them charged to your account at the reception.</t7701> <t7702>The Nature Walk and the Outdoor Historical Costume Parade have been postponed to the day after tomorrow since our infallible Professor Johnny Running Dog has informed us that there will be a change in the weather by then.</t7702>
<t7703>Allow me to remind you of the rest of the activities sponsored by the Gileadian Research Association that you can participate in during this congress as part of the programming for this Twelfth Symposium.</t7703> <t7704>Tomorrow afternoon, Professor Gopal Chatterjee, from the Department of Western Philosophy at the University of Baroda in India, will lecture on "The Krishna and Kali Elements in the State Religion of the Early Gileadian Period," and on Thursday morning, Professor Sieglinda Van Buren, from the Department of Military History at the University of San Antonio, Republic of Texas, will speak.</t7704> <t7705>Professor Van Buren will offer what will undoubtedly be a fascinating illustrated lecture on "The Warsaw Tactic: The Urban Core Encirclement Policy in the Gileadian Civil Wars."</t7705> <t7706>I am sure we will all want to attend.</t7706>
<t7707>I must also remind our keynote speaker, although I am sure it is not necessary, to stick to the time that has been assigned to him, because we want to dedicate a part to questions, and I suppose no one will want to miss lunch, as happened yesterday.</t7707> <t7708>(Laughter.)</t7708>
<t7709>Professor Pieixoto practically needs no introduction as he is well known to all of us, if not personally, at least through his numerous publications.</t7709> <t7710>Among them are "Sumptuary Laws Through the Ages: An Analysis of Documents," and the well-known study "Iran and Gilead: Two Late Twentieth-Century Monotheocracies Seen Through Diaries."</t7710> <t7711>As you all know, he is the co-director, along with Professor Knotly Wade (Knotted Duck), also from Cambridge, of the manuscript we are discussing today and collaborated in its transcription, commentary, and publication.</t7711> <t7712>The title of this talk is "Authentication Issues Related to The Handmaid's Tale."</t7712>
<t7713>Professor Pieixoto.</t7713>
<t7714>(Applause.)</t7714>
<t7715>PIEIXOTO:</t7715> PIEIXOTO:
<t7716>Thank you.</t7716> <t7717>I am sure that we all enjoyed the iced tea at dinner last night and that we are now equally enjoying our fiery president.</t7717> <t7718>I use the word "enjoy" in two senses, excluding, of course, the third, now obsolete.</t7718> <t7719>(Laughter.)</t7719>
<t7720>But let's be serious.</t7720> <t7721>I would like, as the title of this small talk indicates, to consider some of the problems associated with the supposed manuscript that is already well known to all of you and is titled The Handmaid's Tale.</t7721> <t7722>I say supposed because what we have before us is not the article in its original form.</t7722>
<t7723>In strict terms, when we discovered it, it was not a manuscript at all, and it did not have a title.</t7723> <t7724>The inscription "The Handmaid's Tale" was added by Professor Wade, partly as a tribute to the great Geoffrey Chaucer; but those of you who, like me, know Professor Wade more closely, will understand when I say that I am sure all the puns were intentional, especially the one related to the vulgar meaning of the word "tale" being to some extent the foundation of that phase of Gileadean society that our saga deals with.</t7724> <t7725>(Laughter, applause.)</t7725>
<t7726>This article, I dare not use the word document, was discovered at the site of what was once the city of Bangor, in what, in the time before the beginning of the Gileadean regime, had been the state of Maine.</t7726> <t7727>We know that this city was an important stopover of what our author calls "the Women's Metropolitan Train," as some of our humorous historians gave it the nickname "the Chicks' Metropolitan Train."</t7727> <t7728>(Laughter and whistles.)</t7728> <t7729>For this reason, our Association has taken a special interest in it.</t7729>
<t7730>The article in its original state consisted of a metal shoebox, for use by the United States Army, perhaps around nineteen fifty-five.</t7730> <t7731>This fact in itself does not have to be significant, as it is known that these shoeboxes were frequently sold as "army surplus," and therefore may have been scattered.</t7731> <t7732>Inside this shoebox, sealed with adhesive tape like the kind used in the past for postal packages, there were approximately thirty cassettes, of the type that became obsolete around the eighties or nineties, with the advent of compact discs.</t7732>
<t7733>I remind you that this is not the first discovery of this kind.</t7733> <t7734>Without a doubt, you are familiar with the article known as "The Memoirs of A. B.," found in a garage in a suburb of Seattle, and "The Diary of P.," accidentally unearthed during the construction of a new temple near what was once Syracuse, in New York.</t7734>
<t7735>Professor Wade and I were very excited about this new discovery.</t7735>
<t7736>Fortunately, several years earlier, with the help of our resident antique technician, we had reconstructed a device capable of playing such cassettes, and we immediately undertook the careful task of transcription.</t7736>
<t7737>In the collection, there were a total of about thirty cassettes, with varying proportions of music and words.</t7737> <t7738>Generally, each cassette begins with two or three songs, undoubtedly used as camouflage: then the music stops and a voice is heard.</t7738> <t7739>It is the voice of a woman and, according to our phonetics experts, it is the same from beginning to end.</t7739> <t7740>The cassette labels were authentic labels that dated, of course, from a time before the beginning of the first Gileadean era since, under this regime, all that profane music was banned.</t7740> <t7741>For example, there were four cassettes titled "The Golden Years of Elvis Presley," three of</t7741>
<t7742>"Popular Songs of Lithuania," three from "Boy George Takes It Off" and two from</t7742>
<t7743>"The Melodious Violins of Mantovani," as well as some titles for which there was only one cassette: "The Twin Sisters at Carnegie Hall," is one of my favorites.</t7743>
<t7744>Although the labels are authentic, they were not always placed on the cassette with the corresponding songs.</t7744> <t7745>Furthermore, the cassettes were not kept in any special order; they were just thrown at the bottom of the box, and they were not numbered either.</t7745> <t7746>So it fell to Professor Wade and myself to arrange the blocks of dialogue in the order that they seemed to follow; but, as I have said before, the result is based on conjecture and should be considered approximate and subject to further investigation.</t7746>
<t7747>Once we had completed the transcription, and after having to review it several times due to the difficulties posed by the accent, the allusions to unknown things, and the archaisms, we found ourselves obliged to make some decisions regarding the material we had so laboriously obtained.</t7747> <t7748>Several possibilities presented themselves to us.</t7748> <t7749>First of all, the cassettes could be a forgery.</t7749> <t7750>As you know, there have been several cases of forgeries of this type for which publishers have paid large sums, undoubtedly wishing to take advantage of the sensationalism of those accounts.</t7750> <t7751>It seems that certain periods of history quickly become, both for other societies and for those who live through them, a subject of not particularly edifying legends and a motive for hypocritical self-complacency.</t7751> <t7752>If I may make a side comment, I would say that in my opinion we must be cautious in our moral judgments about the Gileadeans.</t7752> <t7753>Surely we have already learned that such judgments are inevitably culture-specific.</t7753>
<t7754>Moreover, the Gileadean society was under strong pressure, demographic and otherwise, and was subject to factors from which we ourselves are free.</t7754>
<t7755>Our mission is not to censor but to understand.</t7755> <t7756>(Applause.)</t7756> <t7757>Setting aside my digression: in any case, it is quite difficult to convincingly falsify a cassette like this one, and the experts who analyzed them assured us that the physical objects themselves were genuine.</t7757> <t7758>By the way, the recording itself, that is, the overlay of the voice on the music, could not have been done in the last hundred or even fifty years.</t7758>
<t7759>Assuming, then, that the cassettes are authentic, what can be said about the nature of the narrative?</t7759> <t7760>Obviously, it could not have been recorded in the same time period it talks about because, if the author is telling the truth, she would not have had access to either a tape recorder or a cassette, nor would she have had anywhere to hide them.</t7760> <t7761>Furthermore, there is a certain reflective quality in her narration that, in my opinion, would rule out simultaneity.</t7761>
<t7762>He possesses a multitude of stored emotions, if not in tranquility, at least post facto.</t7762>
<t7763>We thought that if we could establish the identity of the narrator, we could find a way to explain how this document, allow me to call it that for the sake of brevity, came to light.</t7763> <t7764>For this, we used two lines of investigation.</t7764>
<t7765>First, we tried, using urban plans of Bangor and other remaining documentation, to identify the inhabitants of the house that should have been at the site of the discovery at that time.</t7765> <t7766>We reasoned that it had probably been a "safe house" of the Women's Metropolitan Train of that time, and the author might have hidden it in the attic or the cellar, for example, for weeks or months, during which time she would have had the opportunity to make the recordings.</t7766> <t7767>Of course, there was no indication that would allow us to rule out the possibility that the tapes had been moved to the site in question after being recorded.</t7767> <t7768>We hoped to be able to trace and locate the descendants of the hypothetical occupants who, we hoped, would lead us to other material: diaries, perhaps, or even family anecdotes passed down from generation to generation.</t7768>
<t7769>Unfortunately, this did not lead us to anything.</t7769> <t7770>Perhaps these people, if they really represented a link in the clandestine chain, had been discovered and arrested, in which case any documentation regarding them would have been destroyed.</t7770> <t7771>So we continued with the second line of attack.</t7771> <t7772>We searched the archives of the time, trying to relate historical figures to the individuals who appeared in our author's account.</t7772> <t7773>The archives that have remained from that time are in very poor condition, as the Gileadean regime had the habit of wiping out its own computers and destroying written material after various purges and internal disturbances; but some written material has survived.</t7773> <t7774>Incidentally, part of this material was smuggled into England for propaganda use by the various Women's Protection societies, which at that time proliferated in the British Isles.</t7774>
<t7775>We hold no hope of directly locating the narrator.</t7775> <t7776>Some internal evidence showed us that she was part of the first batch of women recruited for reproductive purposes and assigned to those who requested such services and could claim them, given their belonging to a select minority.</t7776> <t7777>The regime immediately created a reserve of women through the simple tactic of declaring all second marriages and non-marital unions adulterous and arresting the women, and on the basis that they were morally incapable, confiscated the children, who were adopted by childless couples belonging to the upper classes, who were eager to have offspring at any cost.</t7777> <t7778>(During the middle period, this policy was extended to include all marriages not contracted by the state church.)</t7778> <t7779>The men who held high positions in the regime could pick and choose among the women who had demonstrated their reproductive capabilities by having one or more healthy children, a desirable trait in an era of plummeting Caucasian birth rates, a phenomenon observable not only in Gilead but in most northern Caucasian societies of that time.</t7779>
<t7780>The causes of this decline are not entirely clear to us.</t7780> <t7781>Part of the failure regarding reproduction can undoubtedly be attributed to the wide availability of various types of birth control methods, including abortion, during the pre-Gileadean period.</t7781> <t7782>Infertility was partly desired, which can be explained by the different statistics between Caucasians and non-Caucasians, but not in its entirety.</t7782> <t7783>Do I need to remind you that this was the era of the R strain of syphilis and also of the infamous AIDS epidemic which, once it spread throughout the population, eliminated a large part of the young and sexually active population from the reproductive pool?</t7783> <t7784>Stillbirths, miscarriages, and genetic malformations spread and increased, and this trend has been linked to the various accidents at nuclear power plants, shutdowns, and sabotage incidents that characterized the period, as well as chemical leaks and biological warfare substances and toxic waste disposal sites, of which there were several thousand both legal and illegal; in some cases, these materials were simply dumped into the sewer system, and to the uncontrolled use of insecticides, herbicides, and other sprays.</t7784>
<t7785>But whatever the causes were, the effects were notable, and at that moment the regime of Gilead was not the only one to react to them.</t7785> <t7786>In the 1980s, for example, Romania had anticipated Gilead by banning all birth control methods, imposing mandatory pregnancy tests on the female population, and making promotions and salary increases contingent on fertility.</t7786>
<t7787>The need for what I would call birth services was already recognized in the pre-Gileadean period, where they were inadequately carried out through</t7787>
<t7788>"artificial insemination," "fertility clinics," and through the use of "surrogate mothers," who were hired for this purpose.</t7788> <t7789>The regime of Gilead proscribed the first two for being considered irreligious, but legitimized and encouraged the third, understanding that it had biblical precedents; thus, they replaced the common consecutive polygamy of the pre-Gilead period with the older form of simultaneous polygamy practiced both in the early times of the Old Testament and in the old state of Utah during the nineteenth century.</t7789> <t7790>As we know from the study of history, no new system can impose itself on the previous one without incorporating many of its elements, as demonstrated by the existence of pagan elements in medieval Christianity, and the evolution leading to the Russian "K. G. B." from the previous Tsarist secret service; and Gilead was no exception to the rule.</t7790>
<t7791>Their racist principles, for example, were firmly rooted in the pre-Gileadean period, and racist fears provided part of the emotional incentive that allowed the takeover in Gilead to be successful.</t7791>
<t7792>Our author was one among many and should be considered within the general lines of the historical period of which she was a part.</t7792> <t7793>But what else do we know about her, apart from her age, some characteristics that could be attributed to anyone, and her place of residence?</t7793> <t7794>Not much.</t7794> <t7795>She seems to have been a cultured woman, to the extent that one could call a graduate of any university in the United States cultured.</t7795>
<t7796>(Laughter, some whistles.)</t7796> <t7797>But, as you would say, the forests were teeming with specimens of this kind, so it didn't help us much.</t7797> <t7798>She does not provide us with her original name and, indeed, all official records following her admission to the Raquel and Leah Reeducation Center have been destroyed.</t7798> <t7799>The name</t7799>
<t7800>"Defred" does not provide us with any clues since, like "Deglen" and</t7800>
<t7801>"Dewarren" is a patronymic composed of the possessive preposition and the first name of the knight in question.</t7801> <t7802>Such names were adopted by these women once they came into contact with the family of a particular Commander, and they discarded them once they left that family.</t7802>
<t7803>The other names listed in the document are equally useless for the purpose of identification and authentication.</t7803> <t7804>“Luke” and “Nick” mean nothing, just like “Moira” and “Janine.”</t7804> <t7805>The most likely scenario, in any case, is that they were pseudonyms adopted to protect these individuals in case the tapes were discovered.</t7805> <t7806>If that were the case, it would justify our viewpoint that the tapes were recorded within the boundaries of Gilead with the intention of being smuggled out through the Mayday underground network.</t7806>
<t7807>After eliminating the previous possibilities, only one remained for us.</t7807> <t7808>We thought that being able to identify the elusive "Commander" would at least mean some progress.</t7808> <t7809>We considered that such a highly placed individual had probably participated initially in the secret organization Sons of Jacob Pro-Tanks, upon which the philosophy and social structure of Gilead was founded.</t7809> <t7810>This organization was formed shortly after the superpowers agreed to halt the arms race and signed the so-called Spheres of Influence Agreement, which allowed the superpowers freedom of action, without interference, regarding the growing rebellions taking place within their own borders.</t7810>
<t7811>The official records of the Sons of Jacob meetings were destroyed after the Great Purge of the middle period, which disgraced and liquidated some of the early architects of Gilead; but we have some information through the encrypted diary kept by Wilfred Limpkin, one of the sociobiologists of the time.</t7811>
<t7812>(As is well known, the sociobiological theory of natural polygamy was used as a scientific justification for some of the regime's less common practices, just as Darwinism was used by earlier ideologies.)</t7812> <t7813>Thanks to Limpkin's material, we know that there are two possible candidates, namely the two who incorporate the element "Fred" into their names: Frederick R. Waterford and B. Fredrick Judd.</t7813> <t7814>No photographs of them remain, although Limpkin describes the latter as a stiff person and, I quote: "someone for whom work is what is done on the golf course."</t7814> <t7815>(Laughter.)</t7815> <t7816>Limpkin himself did not survive long under the Gilead regime, and if we have his diary, it is only because he foresaw his own end and gave it to his sister-in-law in Calgary.</t7816>
<t7817>Both Waterford and Judd have characteristics that make them worthy of analysis.</t7817> <t7818>Waterford possessed market research knowledge and, according to Limpkin, was responsible for the design of the female uniforms and the idea that the Handmaids should wear red, an idea that seems to have been taken from the uniforms of German prisoners of war who were in Canadian prisoner camps during the Second World War.</t7818> <t7819>He appears to have been the creator of the term "Particicution," for which he was inspired by a very popular exercise program during the last third of the century; nonetheless, the collective ceremony of the rope was suggested by a custom from a seventeenth-century English village.</t7819> <t7820>The term "Salvaging" must also have been his, although by the time of Gilead's establishment, this term, originating from the Philippines, had become a general term to refer to the elimination of political enemies.</t7820> <t7821>As I have said on another occasion, there were very few original or native things in Gilead: its genius lay in synthesis.</t7821>
<t7822>On the other hand, Judd seems to have been less interested in packaging and more in tactics.</t7822> <t7823>It was he who suggested the use of an unknown pamphlet from the "C. IA." about destabilizing a few foreign governments as a strategy manual for the Sons of Jacob, and he also drafted the first lists of "Americans".</t7823>
<t7824>prominent figures of the time.</t7824> <t7825>It is also suspected that he organized the President's Assassination Day, which must have required significant infiltration of the Congress's security systems and without which the Constitution could never have been suspended.</t7825> <t7826>The National Homeland and the project of shipping off the Jews were also his creations, as was the idea of privatizing the Jewish repatriation program, resulting in more than one ship loaded with Jews being sunk in the Atlantic to increase profits.</t7826> <t7827>As far as we know about Judd, this likely did not concern him much.</t7827> <t7828>He belonged to the hardline faction, and Limpkin makes the following observation about him: "Our great mistake was teaching him to read.</t7828> <t7829>We will not make it again."</t7829>
<t7830>It is Judd who is credited with having devised the form, as opposed to the name, of the Particicution ceremony, arguing that it was not only a horrifying and effective way to dispose of subversive elements, but also acted as a valve for the female members of Gilead.</t7830> <t7831>Propitiatory victims have been notably useful throughout history, and for these Handmaids, so rigidly controlled at other times, it must have been very gratifying to be able to tear a man apart with their own hands from time to time.</t7831> <t7832>This practice became so popular and effective that it was regularized during the middle period, when it took place four times a year, during the solstices and equinoxes.</t7832> <t7833>Here there are reminiscences of the fertility rites that were practiced in the early cults of earth goddesses.</t7833> <t7834>As we mentioned in the jury debate yesterday afternoon, Gilead, although undoubtedly patriarchal in form, was also at times matriarchal in content, much like some sectors of the social structure that originated it.</t7834> <t7835>As the architects of Gilead well knew, to impose an effective totalitarian system, or any other system, some benefits and freedoms must be offered, at least to a few privileged ones, in exchange for those that are suppressed.</t7835>
<t7836>In this regard, I find it pertinent to make some comments about the curious female control agency known as the "Aunts."</t7836> <t7837>According to the material provided by Limpkin, Judd was of the opinion from the beginning that the best and most effective way to control women in reproduction and other aspects was through women themselves.</t7837> <t7838>There are several historical precedents for this; in fact, no empire imposed by force or other means has lacked this characteristic: the control of natives through members of their own group.</t7838> <t7839>In the case of Gilead, there were many women eager to serve as Aunts, either out of genuine belief in what they called "traditional values," or for the benefits they could obtain from it.</t7839> <t7840>When power is scarce, it becomes tempting.</t7840> <t7841>It also had a negative incentive: older women, childless or sterile who were not married could serve as Aunts and thus avoid unemployment and the consequent transfer to the infamous Colonies, which were composed of floating populations mainly used as expendable teams for toxic waste disposal, although the lucky ones could be assigned to less dangerous tasks, such as cotton picking or fruit harvesting.</t7841>
<t7842>The idea, then, came from Judd, but the execution bore Waterford's mark.</t7842> <t7843>Which other member of the Sons of Jacob Pro-tanks would have thought of the idea that the Aunts should carry names derived from commercial products used by women in the pre-Gileadean period, and therefore familiar and reassuring to them, such as the names of cosmetic products, cake mixes, frozen desserts, and even medicines?</t7843> <t7844>It was a brilliant stroke and confirms our opinion that, in his prime, Waterford was a man of considerable wit.</t7844> <t7845>As was Judd, in his own style.</t7845>
<t7846>It was known that neither of the two men had had children and therefore could enjoy the right to the Handmaids' offspring.</t7846> <t7847>In the article we wrote together, "The Notion of 'Seed' in the Early Days of Gilead," Professor Wade and I concluded that both men, like many Commanders, had come into contact with a virus causing sterility, developed through secret gene-coupling experiments during the pre-Gileadean period, and that it was intended to be inserted into the caviar substitute consumed by high-ranking Moscow officials.</t7847> <t7848>(The experiment was abandoned after the Spheres of Influence Agreement, because the virus was considered absolutely uncontrollable and also very dangerous for many, although some wanted to spread it throughout the territory of India.)</t7848>
<t7849>In any case, neither Judd nor Waterford were ever married to any woman named "Pam" or "Serena Joy."</t7849> <t7850>This last name seems to have been a malicious invention by our author.</t7850> <t7851>The name of Judd's wife was Bambi Mae, and the name of Waterford's wife was Thelma.</t7851> <t7852>However, the latter had been a television figure, of the type described in the narration.</t7852> <t7853>We learned this through Limpkin's material, which makes several sarcastic observations about it.</t7853>
<t7854>The regime itself took great care to cover up the deviations from orthodoxy by the wives of the privileged classes.</t7854>
<t7855>The evidence tips the scales in favor of Waterford.</t7855> <t7856>We know, for example, that he probably died shortly after the events our author describes, in one of the early purges; he was accused of having liberal tendencies and of being in possession of a significant unauthorized collection of heretical pictorial and literary material, and of harboring a subversive person.</t7856> <t7857>This happened before the regime began holding trials in secret, and therefore they were still televised, so that trial was recorded in England via satellite and is found in the recording archives of our files.</t7857> <t7858>The shots of Waterford are not very good, but clear enough to ensure that his hair was indeed gray.</t7858>
<t7859>As for the subversive person that Waterford was accused of covering up, it could have been "Offred" herself, as her escape might have placed her in that category.</t7859> <t7860>As the very existence of the tapes demonstrates, it is most likely that it was "Nick" who helped "Offred" escape.</t7860> <t7861>The way he did it points to him being a member of the clandestine organization Mayday, which was not the same as the Women's Metropolitan Train, but had relations with it.</t7861> <t7862>The latter was a simple quasi-military rescue operation.</t7862> <t7863>It is known that a number of Mayday components had infiltrated the highest levels of Gileadean power structures and that placing one of its members as Waterford's chauffeur would certainly have been a coup; a double coup, since "Nick" must have also been a member of the Eyes, as was often the case with chauffeurs and personal servants.</t7863> <t7864>Waterford, of course, must have known; but, like all high-level Commanders, he was automatically a director of the Eyes and must not have paid much attention nor let it interfere with his infringement of what he considered minor rules.</t7864> <t7865>Like the vast majority of the early Gilead Commanders who were later purged, he considered his position above any attack.</t7865> <t7866>The style of the mid-Gilead period was more cautious.</t7866>
<t7867>These are our conjectures.</t7867> <t7868>Assuming they are correct, that is, assuming that Waterford was indeed the "Commander," many questions still remain.</t7868> <t7869>Some of them could have been cleared up by our anonymous author, if she had had a different way of seeing things.</t7869> <t7870>If she had had the instinct of a journalist, or a spy, she could have explained many things to us about the functioning of the Gileadean empire.</t7870> <t7871>What wouldn't we give now for twenty pages written from Waterford's private computer!</t7871> <t7872>In any case, we must be grateful for the crumbs that the Goddess of History has seen fit to grant us.</t7872>
<t7873>As for the final fate of our narrator, it remains in the dark.</t7873> <t7874>Was she smuggled across the border of Gilead to what was then Canada, and managed to make her way from there to England?</t7874> <t7875>This would have been an intelligent decision since Canada at that time did not want to antagonize its powerful neighbor and organized raids and extradited refugees.</t7875> <t7876>In that case, why didn't she take the recorded narration with her?</t7876> <t7877>Perhaps her journey was decided at the last moment; perhaps she feared being detained along the way.</t7877> <t7878>On the other hand, she might have been recaptured.</t7878> <t7879>If she did indeed make it to England, why didn't she reveal her story, as many did once they reached the outside world?</t7879> <t7880>She might have feared reprisals against "Luke," assuming he was still alive, which is unlikely, or even against her daughter; because the Gileadean regime was not incapable of such measures, and took them in order to discourage adverse publicity in foreign countries.</t7880> <t7881>It is known that more than one unsuspecting refugee received a hand, an ear, or a foot vacuum-packed and hidden, for example, in a coffee can.</t7881> <t7882>Or perhaps she was among the Handmaids who fled and had difficulty adapting to the outside world, after the sheltered life they had led.</t7882> <t7883>Like them, she may have become a loner.</t7883> <t7884>We do not know.</t7884>
<t7885>We can only make deductions also regarding the motivations of</t7885>
<t7886>"Nick" to organize the escape.</t7886> <t7887>We can assume that once Deglen was discovered, his association with Mayday put him in danger because, as a member of the Eyes, he knew very well that Offred herself would be interrogated.</t7887> <t7888>The penalty for unauthorized sexual activity with a Handmaid was severe, and his status as an Eye did not protect him.</t7888> <t7889>Gileadean society was extremely byzantine, and any transgression could be used against someone by undeclared enemies within the regime.</t7889> <t7890>Of course, he could have killed her, which would have been the smarter path, but the human heart remains a decisive factor, and as we know, both of them thought she might be carrying his child.</t7890> <t7891>What man of the Gileadean period could resist the possibility of being a father, something so imbued with status and so precious?</t7891> <t7892>Instead, he called a rescue team from the Eyes, who may or may not have been genuine, but in any case, they worked under his orders.</t7892> <t7893>This may have also led to his own downfall.</t7893> <t7894>We will never know.</t7894>
<t7895>Did our narrator arrive safe and sound in the outside world and build a new life?</t7895> <t7896>Or was she discovered in her attic hideout, arrested, sent to the Colonies or Jezebel’s, or even executed?</t7896> <t7897>Our document, though eloquent in its own way, does not answer these questions.</t7897> <t7898>We could summon Eurydice from the world of the dead, but we could not get her to respond; and when we turn to look at her, we glimpse her only for a moment, before she slips from our hands and vanishes.</t7898> <t7899>As all historians know, the past is a vast darkness filled with resonances.</t7899> <t7900>From it, some voices may reach us; but what they tell us is imbued with the darkness of the matrix from which they emerge.</t7900> <t7901>And, no matter how hard we try, we cannot always decipher them and illuminate them with the pristine light of our own time.</t7901>
